RN   [47]
RP   FUNCTION IN PHOSPHORYLATION OF ATG9, AND CATALYTIC ACTIVITY.
RX   PubMed=24905091; DOI=10.4161/auto.28971;
RA   Papinski D., Kraft C.;
RT   "Atg1 kinase organizes autophagosome formation by phosphorylating
RT   Atg9.";
RL   Autophagy 10:1338-1340(2014).
CC   -!- FUNCTION: Serine/threonine protein kinase involved in the
CC       cytoplasm to vacuole transport (Cvt) and found to be essential in
CC       autophagy, where it is required for the formation of
CC       autophagosomes. Involved in the clearance of protein aggregates
CC       which cannot be efficiently cleared by the proteasome. Required
CC       for selective autophagic degradation of the nucleus (nucleophagy)
CC       as well as for mitophagy which contributes to regulate
CC       mitochondrial quantity and quality by eliminating the mitochondria
CC       to a basal level to fulfill cellular energy requirements and
CC       preventing excess ROS production. Also involved in endoplasmic
CC       reticulum-specific autophagic process, in selective removal of ER-
CC       associated degradation (ERAD) substrates. Plays a key role in ATG9
CC       and ATG23 cycling through the pre-autophagosomal structure and is
CC       necessary to promote ATG18 binding to ATG9 through phosphorylation
CC       of ATG9. Finally, ATG1 is also required for the maintenance of
CC       cell viability under starvation and for glycogen storage during
CC       stationary phase. Plays a role in genome stability through
CC       suppression of abnormal mitosis under starvation, and in
CC       regulation of filamentous growth. {ECO:0000269|PubMed:10995454,
CC       ECO:0000269|PubMed:11486014, ECO:0000269|PubMed:11689437,
CC       ECO:0000269|PubMed:11904149, ECO:0000269|PubMed:12589048,

CC   -!- CATALYTIC ACTIVITY: ATP + a protein = ADP + a phosphoprotein.
CC       {ECO:0000269|PubMed:24905091}.
CC   -!- ENZYME REGULATION: Activated by hypophosphorylated form of ATG13
CC       (present in nitrogen starvation conditions). Also activated by
CC       autophopsphorylation of Thr-226 and inhibited by phosphorylation
CC       of Ser-34. {ECO:0000269|PubMed:10995454,
CC       ECO:0000269|PubMed:20439775}.
CC   -!- SUBUNIT: Homodimer. Dimerization requires the presence of ATG13.
CC       Forms a ternary complex with ATG13 and ATG17. Interacts also with
CC       ATG11. {ECO:0000269|PubMed:10995454, ECO:0000269|PubMed:11309418,
CC       ECO:0000269|PubMed:18077553, ECO:0000269|PubMed:21712380,
CC       ECO:0000269|PubMed:22778255, ECO:0000269|PubMed:22885598}.

CC       Q12527:ATG11; NbExp=3; IntAct=EBI-2657, EBI-31977;
CC       Q06628:ATG13; NbExp=13; IntAct=EBI-2657, EBI-36188;
CC       P35193:ATG19; NbExp=2; IntAct=EBI-2657, EBI-29291;
CC       P38182:ATG8; NbExp=3; IntAct=EBI-2657, EBI-2684;
CC   -!- SUBCELLULAR LOCATION: Cytoplasm. Preautophagosomal structure
CC       membrane; Peripheral membrane protein. Note=Formes punctate
CC       structures in starvation conditions only when ATG13 and ATG17 were
CC       both present. Localizes to both the isolation membrane (IM) and
CC       the vacuole-isolation membrane contact site (VICS) during IM
CC       expansion. The IM is a membrane sac generated from the pre-
CC       autophagosomal structure that ultimately expands to become a
CC       mature autophagosome.
CC   -!- DOMAIN: The LIR motif is required for the interaction with ATG8
CC       and for the association of ATG1 with autophagosomes.
CC       {ECO:0000269|PubMed:22778255, ECO:0000269|PubMed:22885598}.
CC   -!- PTM: Autophosphorylated at Thr-226 and Ser-390. The
CC       phosphorylation state may play a role in the induction of protein
CC       degradation upon starvation. Phosphorylation at Thr-226 within the
CC       activation loop is required for protein kinase activity whereas
CC       phosphorylation at Ser-34 leads to inhibition of kinase activity.
CC       Phosphorylation of Ser-508 and Ser-515 by PKA is required to
CC       induce autophagy but not for kinase activity.
CC       {ECO:0000269|PubMed:17699586, ECO:0000269|PubMed:20439775,
CC       ECO:0000269|PubMed:21460632, ECO:0000269|PubMed:9224897}.
CC   -!- MISCELLANEOUS: Present with 1070 molecules/cell in log phase SD
CC       medium. {ECO:0000269|PubMed:14562106}.

CC       protein kinase family. APG1/unc-51/ULK1 subfamily.

RP   PHOSPHORYLATION.
RX   PubMed=22727621; DOI=10.1016/j.molcel.2012.05.019;

CC   -!- FUNCTION: Activates the ATG1 kinase in a nutritional condition
CC       dependent manner through the TOR pathway, leading to autophagy.
CC       Required for autophosphorylation of ATG1 at 'Thr-226' and its
CC       dimerization. May also be involved in the regulation of autophagy
CC       through SNF1. Involved in ATG9 and ATG23 cycling through the pre-
CC       autophagosomal structure. Also involved in cytoplasm to vacuole
CC       transport (Cvt) and more specifically in Cvt vesicle formation.
CC       Seems to play a role in the switching machinery regulating the
CC       conversion between the Cvt pathway and autophagy. Finally, ATG13
CC       is also required for glycogen storage during stationary phase.
CC       {ECO:0000269|PubMed:10837477, ECO:0000269|PubMed:10995454,
CC       ECO:0000269|PubMed:11086004, ECO:0000269|PubMed:11486014,
CC       ECO:0000269|PubMed:14723849, ECO:0000269|PubMed:15743910,
CC       ECO:0000269|PubMed:17295840, ECO:0000269|PubMed:17426440,
CC       ECO:0000269|PubMed:17699586, ECO:0000269|PubMed:18077553,
CC       ECO:0000269|PubMed:18287526, ECO:0000269|PubMed:19805182,
CC       ECO:0000269|PubMed:19995911, ECO:0000269|PubMed:20439775,
CC       ECO:0000269|PubMed:20647741, ECO:0000269|PubMed:20855505,
CC       ECO:0000269|PubMed:21468027, ECO:0000269|PubMed:21712380,
CC       ECO:0000269|PubMed:22447937, ECO:0000269|PubMed:22778255,
CC       ECO:0000269|PubMed:22782902, ECO:0000269|PubMed:22885598,
CC       ECO:0000269|PubMed:8224160}.
CC   -!- SUBUNIT: Hypophosphorylated form interacts with ATG1 to form the
CC       ATG1-ATG13 kinase complex. The ATG1-ATG13 complex interacts with
CC       the ATG17-ATG29-ATG31 complex through direct interaction with
CC       ATG17. Interacts with VAC8. {ECO:0000269|PubMed:10837477,
CC       ECO:0000269|PubMed:10995454, ECO:0000269|PubMed:15743910,
CC       ECO:0000269|PubMed:15901835, ECO:0000269|PubMed:18829864,
CC       ECO:0000269|PubMed:19755117, ECO:0000269|PubMed:19805182,
CC       ECO:0000269|PubMed:20439775, ECO:0000269|PubMed:20953146,
CC       ECO:0000269|PubMed:21712380, ECO:0000269|PubMed:22778255,
CC       ECO:0000269|PubMed:22885598, ECO:0000269|PubMed:23219485}.
CC   -!- INTERACTION:
CC       P53104:ATG1; NbExp=13; IntAct=EBI-36188, EBI-2657;
CC       P39968:VAC8; NbExp=5; IntAct=EBI-36188, EBI-20212;
CC   -!- SUBCELLULAR LOCATION: Cytoplasm {ECO:0000269|PubMed:14562095}.
CC       Preautophagosomal structure {ECO:0000269|PubMed:17295840,
CC       ECO:0000269|PubMed:21468027}.
CC   -!- PTM: Phosphorylated; hyperphosphorylated by the TORC1 kinase
CC       complex to repress the induction of autophagy. Starvation and TOR
CC       inactivation results in ATG13 partial dephosphorylation leading to
CC       ATG1-binding. Rephosphorylated by ATG1 during prolonged nitrogen
CC       starvation. Also phosphorylated by PKA. PKA phosphorylation
CC       regulates the association of ATG13 with the PAS. Within this
CC       regulatory network, mitochondrial respiratory deficiency
CC       suppresses autophagic flux. Hyperphosphorylation in rich medium is
CC       impaired in the absence of VAC8. {ECO:0000269|PubMed:10995454,
CC       ECO:0000269|PubMed:17699586, ECO:0000269|PubMed:19805182,
CC       ECO:0000269|PubMed:19995911, ECO:0000269|PubMed:21078689,
CC       ECO:0000269|PubMed:21468027, ECO:0000269|PubMed:21490424,
CC       ECO:0000269|PubMed:21900499, ECO:0000269|PubMed:22447937,
CC       ECO:0000269|PubMed:22727621, ECO:0000269|PubMed:22782902}.
CC   -!- MISCELLANEOUS: Present with 149 molecules/cell in log phase SD
CC       medium. {ECO:0000269|PubMed:14562106}.
CC   -!- SIMILARITY: Belongs to the ATG13 family. Fungi subfamily.
CC       {ECO:0000305}.

CC   -!- FUNCTION: Autophagy-specific protein that functions with ATG13,
CC       ATG29, and CIS1/ATG31 in response to autophagy-inducing signals as
CC       a scaffold to recruit other ATG proteins to organize pre-
CC       autophagosomal structure (PAS) formation. Modulates the timing and
CC       magnitude of the autophagy response, such as the size of the
CC       sequestering vesicles, through interacting with and regulating
CC       ATG1 kinase activity. Plays particularly a role in pexophagy and
CC       nucleophagy. With ATG13, is required for ATG1 activation by
CC       autophosphorylation of 'Thr-226'. Recruits ATG9 to the pre-
CC       autophagosomal structure. Plays also a role in regulation of
CC       filamentous growth. {ECO:0000269|PubMed:10995454,
CC       ECO:0000269|PubMed:11486014, ECO:0000269|PubMed:12048214,
CC       ECO:0000269|PubMed:15743910, ECO:0000269|PubMed:15901835,
CC       ECO:0000269|PubMed:17362880, ECO:0000269|PubMed:17700056,
CC       ECO:0000269|PubMed:18077553, ECO:0000269|PubMed:18287526,
CC       ECO:0000269|PubMed:18701704, ECO:0000269|PubMed:19061865,
CC       ECO:0000269|PubMed:19223769, ECO:0000269|PubMed:19371383,
CC       ECO:0000269|PubMed:19805182, ECO:0000269|PubMed:19995911,
CC       ECO:0000269|PubMed:20439775, ECO:0000269|PubMed:20729555,
CC       ECO:0000269|PubMed:21712380, ECO:0000269|PubMed:22768199,
CC       ECO:0000269|PubMed:23169651}.
CC   -!- SUBUNIT: Forms a complex with ATG13, ATG29 and CIS1/ATG31. The
CC       ATG17-ATG29-ATG31 complex interacts with the ATG1-ATG13 complex.
CC       Forms a complex with SNX4 and ATG20. Interacts with ATG11 and the
CC       conserved oligomeric Golgi (COG) complex subunits COG1, COG3 and
CC       COG4. {ECO:0000269|PubMed:10995454, ECO:0000269|PubMed:12048214,
CC       ECO:0000269|PubMed:15659643, ECO:0000269|PubMed:15743910,
CC       ECO:0000269|PubMed:15901835, ECO:0000269|PubMed:17362880,
CC       ECO:0000269|PubMed:18287526, ECO:0000269|PubMed:19371383,
CC       ECO:0000269|PubMed:19755117, ECO:0000269|PubMed:19805182,
CC       ECO:0000269|PubMed:19995911, ECO:0000269|PubMed:20065092,
CC       ECO:0000269|PubMed:21712380, ECO:0000269|PubMed:22778255,
CC       ECO:0000269|PubMed:22885598}.
CC   -!- INTERACTION:
CC       Q12421:ATG31; NbExp=4; IntAct=EBI-30856, EBI-34768;
CC       P53267:DAM1; NbExp=3; IntAct=EBI-30856, EBI-23268;
CC       P47057:SNX4; NbExp=3; IntAct=EBI-30856, EBI-17610;
CC   -!- SUBCELLULAR LOCATION: Cytoplasm. Preautophagosomal structure
CC       membrane; Peripheral membrane protein.
CC   -!- MISCELLANEOUS: Present with 358 molecules/cell in log phase SD
CC       medium. {ECO:0000269|PubMed:14562106}.
CC   -!- SIMILARITY: Belongs to the ATG17 family. {ECO:0000305}.

CC   -!- FUNCTION: Beta subunit of the SNF1 kinase complex, which is
CC       required for transcriptional, metabolic, and developmental
CC       adaptations in response to glucose limitation. Has a structural
CC       role, mediating heterotrimer formation, and a regulatory role,
CC       defining carbon source-regulated subcellular location and
CC       substrate specificity of the SNF1 kinase complex. Promotes the
CC       PKA-regulated relocalization of the SNF1 kinase complex to the
CC       vacuolar membrane in response to various types of carbon stress.
CC       {ECO:0000269|PubMed:10990457, ECO:0000269|PubMed:8088514}.
CC   -!- SUBUNIT: Component of the SNF1 kinase complex, a heterotrimeric
CC       complex composed of the catalytic alpha subunit SNF1, one of the
CC       three related beta subunits SIP1, SIP2 or GAL83, and the
CC       regulatory gamma subunit SNF4. The beta subunit serves as a bridge
CC       between the catalytic and the regulatory subunit. Interacts (via
CC       KIS domain) with SNF1. Interacts (via ASC domain) with SNF4.
CC       {ECO:0000269|PubMed:12393914, ECO:0000269|PubMed:1496382,
CC       ECO:0000269|PubMed:7813428, ECO:0000269|PubMed:9121458}.
CC   -!- INTERACTION:
CC       P12904:SNF4; NbExp=4; IntAct=EBI-17179, EBI-17537;
CC   -!- SUBCELLULAR LOCATION: Cytoplasm {ECO:0000269|PubMed:11331606,
CC       ECO:0000269|PubMed:14966266}. Vacuole membrane
CC       {ECO:0000269|PubMed:11331606, ECO:0000269|PubMed:14966266};
CC       Peripheral membrane protein {ECO:0000269|PubMed:11331606,
CC       ECO:0000269|PubMed:14966266}; Cytoplasmic side
CC       {ECO:0000269|PubMed:11331606, ECO:0000269|PubMed:14966266}.
CC       Note=Resides in the cytosol during growth in glucose and
CC       relocalizes to the vacuolar membrane in response to carbon stress.
CC       {ECO:0000269|PubMed:14966266}.
CC   -!- PTM: Phosphorylated by SNF1 in vitro. {ECO:0000269|PubMed:1496382,
CC       ECO:0000269|PubMed:7785324, ECO:0000269|PubMed:7813428}.
CC   -!- MISCELLANEOUS: Present with 623 molecules/cell in log phase SD
CC       medium. {ECO:0000269|PubMed:14562106}.
CC   -!- SIMILARITY: Belongs to the 5'-AMP-activated protein kinase beta
CC       subunit family. {ECO:0000305}.
